# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Modal

On this page

# Modal

The Modal component is a simple way to present content above an enclosing view.
To render the `Modal` above other components, you'll need to wrap it with the [`Portal`](/react-native-paper/docs/components/Portal) component.
Note that this modal is NOT accessible by default; if you need an accessible modal, please use the React Native Modal.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/modal.gif)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { Modal, Portal, Text, Button, PaperProvider } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [visible, setVisible] = React.useState(false);  
  
  const showModal = () => setVisible(true);  
  const hideModal = () => setVisible(false);  
  const containerStyle = {backgroundColor: 'white', padding: 20};  
  
  return (  
    <PaperProvider>  
      <Portal>  
        <Modal visible={visible} onDismiss={hideModal} contentContainerStyle={containerStyle}>  
          <Text>Example Modal.  Click outside this area to dismiss.</Text>  
        </Modal>  
      </Portal>  
      <Button style={{marginTop: 30}} onPress={showModal}>  
        Show  
      </Button>  
    </PaperProvider>  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### dismissable[​](#dismissable "Direct link to dismissable")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `true`

Determines whether clicking outside the modal dismisses it.

### dismissableBackButton[​](#dismissablebackbutton "Direct link to dismissableBackButton")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `dismissable`

Determines whether clicking Android hardware back button dismisses the dialog.

### onDismiss[​](#ondismiss "Direct link to onDismiss")

Type: `() => void`

Default value: `() => {}`

Callback that is called when the user dismisses the modal.

### overlayAccessibilityLabel[​](#overlayaccessibilitylabel "Direct link to overlayAccessibilityLabel")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'Close modal'`

Accessibility label for the overlay. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps outside the modal.

### visible[​](#visible "Direct link to visible")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `false`

Determines Whether the modal is visible.

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

Content of the `Modal`.

### contentContainerStyle[​](#contentcontainerstyle "Direct link to contentContainerStyle")

Type: `Animated.WithAnimatedValue<StyleProp<ViewStyle>>`

Style for the content of the modal

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

Style for the wrapper of the modal.
Use this prop to change the default wrapper style or to override safe area insets with marginTop and marginBottom.

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'modal'`

testID to be used on tests.

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

| mode | backgroundColor |
| --- | --- |
| - | theme.colors.backdrop |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<Modal theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Portal/

On this page

# Portal

Portal allows rendering a component at a different place in the parent tree.
You can use it to render content which should appear above other elements, similar to `Modal`.
It requires a [`Portal.Host`](/react-native-paper/docs/components/Portal/PortalHost) component to be rendered somewhere in the parent tree.
Note that if you're using the `Provider` component, this already includes a `Portal.Host`.

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { Portal, Text } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => (  
  <Portal>  
    <Text>This is rendered at a different place</Text>  
  </Portal>  
);  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

Content of the `Portal`.

### theme (required)[​](#theme-required "Direct link to theme (required)")

Type: `InternalTheme`

## More Examples[​](#more-examples "Direct link to More Examples")

Toggle to grab more examples

* [Comprehensive Portal example](https://snack.expo.dev/@react-native-paper/more-examples---comprehensive-portal-example)

* [Usage](#usage)
* [Props](#props)
  + [children (required)](#children-required)
  + [theme (required)](#theme-required)
* [More Examples](#more-examples)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Portal/PortalHost

On this page

# Portal.Host

Portal host renders all of its children `Portal` elements.
For example, you can wrap a screen in `Portal.Host` to render items above the screen.
If you're using the `Provider` component, it already includes `Portal.Host`.

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { Text } from 'react-native';  
import { Portal } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => (  
  <Portal.Host>  
    <Text>Content of the app</Text>  
  </Portal.Host>  
);  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

Here any `Portal` elements under `<App />` are rendered alongside `<App />` and will appear above `<App />` like a `Modal`.

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

* [Usage](#usage)
* [Props](#props)
  + [children (required)](#children-required)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/ProgressBar

On this page

# ProgressBar

Progress bar is an indicator used to present progress of some activity in the app.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/progress-bar.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { ProgressBar, MD3Colors } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => (  
  <ProgressBar progress={0.5} color={MD3Colors.error50} />  
);  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### animatedValue[​](#animatedvalue "Direct link to animatedValue")

Type: `number`

Animated value (between 0 and 1). This tells the progress bar to rely on this value to animate it.
Note: It should not be used in parallel with the `progress` prop.

### progress[​](#progress "Direct link to progress")

Type: `number`

Default value: `0`

Progress value (between 0 and 1).
Note: It should not be used in parallel with the `animatedValue` prop.

### color[​](#color "Direct link to color")

Type: `string`

Color of the progress bar. The background color will be calculated based on this but you can change it by passing `backgroundColor` to `style` prop.

### indeterminate[​](#indeterminate "Direct link to indeterminate")

Type: `boolean`

If the progress bar will show indeterminate progress.

### visible[​](#visible "Direct link to visible")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `true`

Whether to show the ProgressBar (true, the default) or hide it (false).

### fillStyle[​](#fillstyle "Direct link to fillStyle")

Type: `Animated.WithAnimatedValue<StyleProp<ViewStyle>>`

Style of filled part of the ProgresBar.

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'progress-bar'`

testID to be used on tests.

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

| mode | tintColor | trackTintColor |
| --- | --- | --- |
| - | theme.colors.primary | theme.colors.surfaceVariant |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<ProgressBar theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

On this page

# RadioButton

Radio buttons allow the selection a single option from a set.

* Android (enabled)
* Android (disabled)
* iOS (enabled)
* iOS (disabled)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/radio-enabled.android.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/radio-disabled.android.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/radio-enabled.ios.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/radio-disabled.ios.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { View } from 'react-native';  
import { RadioButton } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [checked, setChecked] = React.useState('first');  
  
  return (  
    <View>  
      <RadioButton  
        value="first"  
        status={ checked === 'first' ? 'checked' : 'unchecked' }  
        onPress={() => setChecked('first')}  
      />  
      <RadioButton  
        value="second"  
        status={ checked === 'second' ? 'checked' : 'unchecked' }  
        onPress={() => setChecked('second')}  
      />  
    </View>  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### value (required)[​](#value-required "Direct link to value (required)")

Type: `string`

Value of the radio button

### status[​](#status "Direct link to status")

Type: `'checked' | 'unchecked'`

Status of radio button.

### disabled[​](#disabled "Direct link to disabled")

Type: `boolean`

Whether radio is disabled.

### onPress[​](#onpress "Direct link to onPress")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Function to execute on press.

### uncheckedColor[​](#uncheckedcolor "Direct link to uncheckedColor")

Type: `string`

Custom color for unchecked radio.

### color[​](#color "Direct link to color")

Type: `string`

Custom color for radio.

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

testID to be used on tests.

  + [disabled](#disabled)
  + [onPress](#onpress)
  + [uncheckedColor](#uncheckedcolor)
  + [color](#color)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/RadioButton/RadioButtonGroup

On this page

# RadioButton.Group

Radio button group allows to control a group of radio buttons.

* Android
* iOS

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/radio-button-group-android.gif)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/radio-button-group-ios.gif)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { View } from 'react-native';  
import { RadioButton, Text } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [value, setValue] = React.useState('first');  
  
  return (  
    <RadioButton.Group onValueChange={newValue => setValue(newValue)} value={value}>  
      <View>  
        <Text>First</Text>  
        <RadioButton value="first" />  
      </View>  
      <View>  
        <Text>Second</Text>  
        <RadioButton value="second" />  
      </View>  
    </RadioButton.Group>  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### onValueChange (required)[​](#onvaluechange-required "Direct link to onValueChange (required)")

Type: `(value: string) => void`

Function to execute on selection change.

### value (required)[​](#value-required "Direct link to value (required)")

Type: `string`

Value of the currently selected radio button.

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

React elements containing radio buttons.

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/RadioButton/RadioButtonItem

On this page

# RadioButton.Item

RadioButton.Item allows you to press the whole row (item) instead of only the RadioButton.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/radio-item.ios.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { RadioButton } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [value, setValue] = React.useState('first');  
  
  return (  
    <RadioButton.Group onValueChange={value => setValue(value)} value={value}>  
      <RadioButton.Item label="First item" value="first" />  
      <RadioButton.Item label="Second item" value="second" />  
    </RadioButton.Group>  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### value (required)[​](#value-required "Direct link to value (required)")

Type: `string`

Value of the radio button.

### label (required)[​](#label-required "Direct link to label (required)")

Type: `string`

Label to be displayed on the item.

### disabled[​](#disabled "Direct link to disabled")

Type: `boolean`

Whether radio is disabled.

### background[​](#background "Direct link to background")

Type: `PressableAndroidRippleConfig`

Type of background drawabale to display the feedback (Android).
<https://reactnative.dev/docs/pressable#rippleconfig>

### onPress[​](#onpress "Direct link to onPress")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Function to execute on press.

### onLongPress[​](#onlongpress "Direct link to onLongPress")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Function to execute on long press.

### accessibilityLabel[​](#accessibilitylabel "Direct link to accessibilityLabel")

Type: `string`

Default value: `label`

Accessibility label for the touchable. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the touchable.

### uncheckedColor[​](#uncheckedcolor "Direct link to uncheckedColor")

Type: `string`

Custom color for unchecked radio.

### color[​](#color "Direct link to color")

Type: `string`

Custom color for radio.

### rippleColor[​](#ripplecolor "Direct link to rippleColor")

Type: `ColorValue`

Color of the ripple effect.

### status[​](#status "Direct link to status")

Type: `'checked' | 'unchecked'`

Status of radio button.

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

Additional styles for container View.

### labelStyle[​](#labelstyle "Direct link to labelStyle")

Type: [`StyleProp<TextStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/text-style-props)

Style that is passed to Label element.

### labelVariant Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#labelvariant--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to labelvariant--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `unknown`

Default value: `'bodyLarge'`

Label text variant defines appropriate text styles for type role and its size.
Available variants:

Display: `displayLarge`, `displayMedium`, `displaySmall`

Headline: `headlineLarge`, `headlineMedium`, `headlineSmall`

Title: `titleLarge`, `titleMedium`, `titleSmall`

Label: `labelLarge`, `labelMedium`, `labelSmall`

Body: `bodyLarge`, `bodyMedium`, `bodySmall`

### labelMaxFontSizeMultiplier[​](#labelmaxfontsizemultiplier "Direct link to labelMaxFontSizeMultiplier")

Type: `number`

Specifies the largest possible scale a label font can reach.

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

testID to be used on tests.

### mode[​](#mode "Direct link to mode")

Type: `'android' | 'ios'`

Whether `<RadioButton.Android />` or `<RadioButton.IOS />` should be used.
Left undefined `<RadioButton />` will be used.

### position[​](#position "Direct link to position")

Type: `'leading' | 'trailing'`

Default value: `'trailing'`

Radio button control position.

### hitSlop[​](#hitslop "Direct link to hitSlop")

Type: `TouchableRippleProps['hitSlop']`

Sets additional distance outside of element in which a press can be detected.

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Searchbar

# Searchbar

Searchbar is a simple input box where users can type search queries.

* bar
* view

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/searchbar.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/searchbar-view.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { Searchbar } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [searchQuery, setSearchQuery] = React.useState('');  
  
  return (  
    <Searchbar  
      placeholder="Search"  
      onChangeText={setSearchQuery}  
      value={searchQuery}  
    />  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### placeholder[​](#placeholder "Direct link to placeholder")

Type: `string`

Hint text shown when the input is empty.

### value (required)[​](#value-required "Direct link to value (required)")

Type: `string`

The value of the text input.

### onChangeText[​](#onchangetext "Direct link to onChangeText")

Type: `(query: string) => void`

Callback that is called when the text input's text changes.

### mode Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#mode--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to mode--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `'bar' | 'view'`

Default value: `'bar'`

Search layout mode, the default value is "bar".

### icon[​](#icon "Direct link to icon")

Type: [`IconSource`](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/blob/main/src/components/Icon.tsx#L16)

Icon name for the left icon button (see `onIconPress`).

### iconColor[​](#iconcolor "Direct link to iconColor")

Type: `string`

Custom color for icon, default will be derived from theme

### rippleColor[​](#ripplecolor "Direct link to rippleColor")

Type: `ColorValue`

Color of the ripple effect.

### onIconPress[​](#oniconpress "Direct link to onIconPress")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Callback to execute if we want the left icon to act as button.

### onClearIconPress[​](#oncleariconpress "Direct link to onClearIconPress")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Callback to execute if we want to add custom behaviour to close icon button.

### searchAccessibilityLabel[​](#searchaccessibilitylabel "Direct link to searchAccessibilityLabel")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'search'`

Accessibility label for the button. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the button.

### clearIcon[​](#clearicon "Direct link to clearIcon")

Type: [`IconSource`](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/blob/main/src/components/Icon.tsx#L16)

Custom icon for clear button, default will be icon close. It's visible when `loading` is set to `false`.
In v5.x with theme version 3, `clearIcon` is visible only if `right` prop is not defined.

### clearAccessibilityLabel[​](#clearaccessibilitylabel "Direct link to clearAccessibilityLabel")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'clear'`

Accessibility label for the button. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the button.

### traileringIcon Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#traileringicon--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to traileringicon--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: [`IconSource`](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/blob/main/src/components/Icon.tsx#L16)

Icon name for the right trailering icon button.
Works only when `mode` is set to "bar". It won't be displayed if `loading` is set to `true`.

### traileringIconColor Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#traileringiconcolor--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to traileringiconcolor--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `string`

Custom color for the right trailering icon, default will be derived from theme

### traileringRippleColor Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#traileringripplecolor--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to traileringripplecolor--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `ColorValue`

Color of the trailering icon ripple effect.

### onTraileringIconPress Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#ontraileringiconpress--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to ontraileringiconpress--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Callback to execute on the right trailering icon button press.

### traileringIconAccessibilityLabel[​](#traileringiconaccessibilitylabel "Direct link to traileringIconAccessibilityLabel")

Type: `string`

Accessibility label for the right trailering icon button. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the button.

### right Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#right--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to right--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `(props: {
color: string;
style: Style;
testID: string;
}) => React.ReactNode`

Callback which returns a React element to display on the right side.
Works only when `mode` is set to "bar".

### showDivider Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#showdivider--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to showdivider--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `true`

Whether to show `Divider` at the bottom of the search.
Works only when `mode` is set to "view". True by default.

### elevation Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#elevation--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to elevation--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `0 | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | Animated.Value`

Default value: `0`

Changes Searchbar shadow and background on iOS and Android.

### inputStyle[​](#inputstyle "Direct link to inputStyle")

Type: [`StyleProp<TextStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/text-style-props)

Set style of the TextInput component inside the searchbar

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: `Animated.WithAnimatedValue<StyleProp<ViewStyle>>`

### loading[​](#loading "Direct link to loading")

Type: `Boolean`

Default value: `false`

Custom flag for replacing clear button with activity indicator.

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'search-bar'`

TestID used for testing purposes

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

| mode | backgroundColor | placeholderTextColor | textColor | selectionColor | iconColor | trailingIconColor | dividerColor |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| - | theme.colors.elevation.level3 | theme.colors.onSurface | theme.colors.onSurfaceVariant | theme.colors.primary | theme.colors.onSurfaceVariant | theme.colors.onSurfaceVariant | theme.colors.outline |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<Searchbar theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/SegmentedButtons/

On this page

# SegmentedButtons

Segmented buttons can be used to select options, switch views or sort elements.

* single select
* multiselect

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/segmented-button-single-select.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/segmented-button-multi-select.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { SafeAreaView, StyleSheet } from 'react-native';  
import { SegmentedButtons } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [value, setValue] = React.useState('');  
  
  return (  
    <SafeAreaView style={styles.container}>  
      <SegmentedButtons  
        value={value}  
        onValueChange={setValue}  
        buttons={[  
          {  
            value: 'walk',  
            label: 'Walking',  
          },  
          {  
            value: 'train',  
            label: 'Transit',  
          },  
          { value: 'drive', label: 'Driving' },  
        ]}  
      />  
    </SafeAreaView>  
  );  
};  
  
const styles = StyleSheet.create({  
  container: {  
    flex: 1,  
    alignItems: 'center',  
  },  
});  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### buttons (required)[​](#buttons-required "Direct link to buttons (required)")

Type: `{
value: T;
icon?: IconSource;
disabled?: boolean;
accessibilityLabel?: string;
checkedColor?: string;
uncheckedColor?: string;
onPress?: (event: GestureResponderEvent) => void;
label?: string;
showSelectedCheck?: boolean;
style?: StyleProp<ViewStyle>;
labelStyle?: StyleProp<TextStyle>;
testID?: string;
}[]`

Buttons to display as options in toggle button.
Button should contain the following properties:

* `value`: value of button (required)
* `icon`: icon to display for the item
* `disabled`: whether the button is disabled
* `accessibilityLabel`: acccessibility label for the button. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the button.
* `checkedColor`: custom color for checked Text and Icon
* `uncheckedColor`: custom color for unchecked Text and Icon
* `onPress`: callback that is called when button is pressed
* `label`: label text of the button
* `showSelectedCheck`: show optional check icon to indicate selected state
* `style`: pass additional styles for the button
* `testID`: testID to be used on tests

### density[​](#density "Direct link to density")

Type: `'regular' | 'small' | 'medium' | 'high'`

Density is applied to the height, to allow usage in denser UIs

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

* checked
* unchecked
* disabled

| mode | backgroundColor | textColor | borderColor |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| - | theme.colors.secondaryContainer | theme.colors.onSecondaryContainer | theme.colors.primary |

| mode | backgroundColor | textColor | borderColor |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| - |  | theme.colors.onSurface | theme.colors.outline |

| mode | backgroundColor | textColor | borderColor |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| - |  | theme.colors.onSurfaceDisabled | theme.colors.surfaceDisabled |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<SegmentedButtons theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Snackbar

On this page

# Snackbar

Snackbars provide brief feedback about an operation through a message rendered at the bottom of the container in which it's wrapped.

Note: To display it as a popup, regardless of the parent's position, wrap it with a `Portal` component – refer to the example in the "More Examples` section.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/snackbar.gif)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { View, StyleSheet } from 'react-native';  
import { Button, Snackbar } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [visible, setVisible] = React.useState(false);  
  
  const onToggleSnackBar = () => setVisible(!visible);  
  
  const onDismissSnackBar = () => setVisible(false);  
  
  return (  
    <View style={styles.container}>  
      <Button onPress={onToggleSnackBar}>{visible ? 'Hide' : 'Show'}</Button>  
      <Snackbar  
        visible={visible}  
        onDismiss={onDismissSnackBar}  
        action={{  
          label: 'Undo',  
          onPress: () => {  
            // Do something  
          },  
        }}>  
        Hey there! I'm a Snackbar.  
      </Snackbar>  
    </View>  
  );  
};  
  
const styles = StyleSheet.create({  
  container: {  
    flex: 1,  
    justifyContent: 'space-between',  
  },  
});  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### visible (required)[​](#visible-required "Direct link to visible (required)")

Type: `boolean`

Whether the Snackbar is currently visible.

### action[​](#action "Direct link to action")

Type: `$RemoveChildren<typeof Button> & {
label: string;
}`

Label and press callback for the action button. It should contain the following properties:

* `label` - Label of the action button
* `onPress` - Callback that is called when action button is pressed.

### icon Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#icon--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to icon--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: [`IconSource`](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/blob/main/src/components/Icon.tsx#L16)

Icon to display when `onIconPress` is defined. Default will be `close` icon.

### rippleColor Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#ripplecolor--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to ripplecolor--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `ColorValue`

Color of the ripple effect.

### onIconPress Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#oniconpress--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to oniconpress--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `() => void`

Function to execute on icon button press. The icon button appears only when this prop is specified.

### iconAccessibilityLabel Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#iconaccessibilitylabel--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to iconaccessibilitylabel--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'Close icon'`

Accessibility label for the icon button. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the button.

### duration[​](#duration "Direct link to duration")

Type: `number`

Default value: `7000`

The duration for which the Snackbar is shown.

### onDismiss (required)[​](#ondismiss-required "Direct link to onDismiss (required)")

Type: `() => void`

Callback called when Snackbar is dismissed. The `visible` prop needs to be updated when this is called.

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

Text content of the Snackbar.

### elevation Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#elevation--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to elevation--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `0 | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | Animated.Value`

Default value: `2`

Changes Snackbar shadow and background on iOS and Android.

### maxFontSizeMultiplier[​](#maxfontsizemultiplier "Direct link to maxFontSizeMultiplier")

Type: `number`

Specifies the largest possible scale a text font can reach.

### wrapperStyle[​](#wrapperstyle "Direct link to wrapperStyle")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

Style for the wrapper of the snackbar

### contentStyle[​](#contentstyle "Direct link to contentStyle")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

Style for the content of the snackbar

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: `Animated.WithAnimatedValue<StyleProp<ViewStyle>>`

### ref[​](#ref "Direct link to ref")

Type: `React.RefObject<View>`

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

TestID used for testing purposes

## More Examples[​](#more-examples "Direct link to More Examples")

Toggle to grab more examples

* [Snackbar rendered regardless of the parent positioning](https://snack.expo.dev/@react-native-paper/more-examples---snackbar-rendered-regardless-of-the-parent-positioning)

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

| mode | iconColor |
| --- | --- |
| - | theme.colors.inverseOnSurface |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<Snackbar theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Surface

On this page

# Surface

Surface is a basic container that can give depth to an element with elevation shadow.
On dark theme with `adaptive` mode, surface is constructed by also placing a semi-transparent white overlay over a component surface.
See [Dark Theme](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#dark-theme) for more information.
Overlay and shadow can be applied by specifying the `elevation` property both on Android and iOS.

* elevated
* flat

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/surface-elevated-full-width.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/surface-flat-full-width.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { Surface, Text } from 'react-native-paper';  
import { StyleSheet } from 'react-native';  
  
const MyComponent = () => (  
  <Surface style={styles.surface} elevation={4}>  
     <Text>Surface</Text>  
  </Surface>  
);  
  
export default MyComponent;  
  
const styles = StyleSheet.create({  
  surface: {  
    padding: 8,  
    height: 80,  
    width: 80,  
    alignItems: 'center',  
    justifyContent: 'center',  
  },  
});
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

Content of the `Surface`.

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: `Animated.WithAnimatedValue<StyleProp<ViewStyle>>`

### elevation Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#elevation--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to elevation--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `0 | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | Animated.Value`

Default value: `1`

Changes shadows and background on iOS and Android.
Used to create UI hierarchy between components.

Note: If `mode` is set to `flat`, Surface doesn't have a shadow.

Note: In version 2 the `elevation` prop was accepted via `style` prop i.e. `style={{ elevation: 4 }}`.
It's no longer supported with theme version 3 and you should use `elevation` property instead.

### mode Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#mode--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to mode--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `'flat' | 'elevated'`

Default value: `'elevated'`

Mode of the Surface.

* `elevated` - Surface with a shadow and background color corresponding to set `elevation` value.
* `flat` - Surface without a shadow, with the background color corresponding to set `elevation` value.

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

Default value: `'surface'`

TestID used for testing purposes

### ref[​](#ref "Direct link to ref")

Type: `React.RefObject<View>`

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

| mode | backgroundColor |
| --- | --- |
| flat | theme.colors.elevation[elevation] |
| elevated | theme.colors.elevation[elevation] |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<Surface theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

  + [children (required)](#children-required)
  + [style](#style)

  + [mode Available in v5.x with theme version 3](#mode--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3)
  + [theme](#theme)

  + [ref](#ref)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Switch/

On this page

# Switch

Switch is a visual toggle between two mutually exclusive states — on and off.

* Android (enabled)
* Android (disabled)
* iOS (enabled)
* iOS (disabled)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/switch-enabled.android.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/switch-disabled.android.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/switch-enabled.ios.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/switch-disabled.ios.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { Switch } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [isSwitchOn, setIsSwitchOn] = React.useState(false);  
  
  const onToggleSwitch = () => setIsSwitchOn(!isSwitchOn);  
  
  return <Switch value={isSwitchOn} onValueChange={onToggleSwitch} />;  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### disabled[​](#disabled "Direct link to disabled")

Type: `boolean`

Disable toggling the switch.

### value[​](#value "Direct link to value")

Type: `boolean`

Value of the switch, true means 'on', false means 'off'.

### color[​](#color "Direct link to color")

Type: `string`

Custom color for switch.

### onValueChange[​](#onvaluechange "Direct link to onValueChange")

Type: `Function`

Callback called with the new value when it changes.

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

  + [disabled](#disabled)
  + [value](#value)
  + [color](#color)
  + [onValueChange](#onvaluechange)
  + [style](#style)
  + [theme](#theme)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Text/

On this page

# Text

Typography component showing styles complied with passed `variant` prop and supported by the type system.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/typography.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { Text } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => (  
  <>  
    <Text variant="displayLarge">Display Large</Text>  
    <Text variant="displayMedium">Display Medium</Text>  
    <Text variant="displaySmall">Display small</Text>  
  
    <Text variant="headlineLarge">Headline Large</Text>  
    <Text variant="headlineMedium">Headline Medium</Text>  
    <Text variant="headlineSmall">Headline Small</Text>  
  
    <Text variant="titleLarge">Title Large</Text>  
    <Text variant="titleMedium">Title Medium</Text>  
    <Text variant="titleSmall">Title Small</Text>  
  
    <Text variant="bodyLarge">Body Large</Text>  
    <Text variant="bodyMedium">Body Medium</Text>  
    <Text variant="bodySmall">Body Small</Text>  
  
    <Text variant="labelLarge">Label Large</Text>  
    <Text variant="labelMedium">Label Medium</Text>  
    <Text variant="labelSmall">Label Small</Text>  
 </>  
);  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### Text props[​](#text-props "Direct link to Text props")

*Extends:* [`...Text props`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/text#props)

### variant Available in v5.x with theme version 3[​](#variant--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3 "Direct link to variant--available-in-v5x-with-theme-version-3")

Type: `VariantProp<T>`

Variant defines appropriate text styles for type role and its size.
Available variants:

Display: `displayLarge`, `displayMedium`, `displaySmall`

Headline: `headlineLarge`, `headlineMedium`, `headlineSmall`

Title: `titleLarge`, `titleMedium`, `titleSmall`

Label: `labelLarge`, `labelMedium`, `labelSmall`

Body: `bodyLarge`, `bodyMedium`, `bodySmall`

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: [`StyleProp<TextStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/text-style-props)

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

| mode | textColor |
| --- | --- |
| - | theme.colors.onSurface |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<Text theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

  + [theme](#theme)
  + [style](#style)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/TextInput/

On this page

# TextInput

A component to allow users to input text.

* flat (focused)
* flat (disabled)
* outlined (focused)
* outlined (disabled)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/textinput-flat.focused.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/textinput-flat.disabled.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/textinput-outlined.focused.png)

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/textinput-outlined.disabled.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { TextInput } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [text, setText] = React.useState("");  
  
  return (  
    <TextInput  
      label="Email"  
      value={text}  
      onChangeText={text => setText(text)}  
    />  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### TextInput props[​](#textinput-props "Direct link to TextInput props")

*Extends:* [`...TextInput props`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/textinput#props)

### mode[​](#mode "Direct link to mode")

Type: `'flat' | 'outlined'`

Default value: `'flat'`

Mode of the TextInput.

* `flat` - flat input with an underline.
* `outlined` - input with an outline.

In `outlined` mode, the background color of the label is derived from `colors?.background` in theme or the `backgroundColor` style.
This component render TextInputOutlined or TextInputFlat based on that props

### left[​](#left "Direct link to left")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

The adornment placed on the left side of the input. It can be either `TextInput.Icon` or `TextInput.Affix`.

### right[​](#right "Direct link to right")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

The adornment placed on the right side of the input. It can be either `TextInput.Icon` or `TextInput.Affix`.

### disabled[​](#disabled "Direct link to disabled")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `false`

If true, user won't be able to interact with the component.

### label[​](#label "Direct link to label")

Type: `TextInputLabelProp`

The text or component to use for the floating label.

### placeholder[​](#placeholder "Direct link to placeholder")

Type: `string`

Placeholder for the input.

### error[​](#error "Direct link to error")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `false`

Whether to style the TextInput with error style.

### onChangeText[​](#onchangetext "Direct link to onChangeText")

Type: `Function`

Callback that is called when the text input's text changes. Changed text is passed as an argument to the callback handler.

### selectionColor[​](#selectioncolor "Direct link to selectionColor")

Type: `string`

Selection color of the input. On iOS, it sets both the selection color and cursor color.
On Android, it sets only the selection color.

### cursorColor Android only[​](#cursorcolor--android-only "Direct link to cursorcolor--android-only")

Type: `string`

Cursor (or "caret") color of the input on Android.
This property has no effect on iOS.

### underlineColor[​](#underlinecolor "Direct link to underlineColor")

Type: `string`

Inactive underline color of the input.

### activeUnderlineColor[​](#activeunderlinecolor "Direct link to activeUnderlineColor")

Type: `string`

Active underline color of the input.

### outlineColor[​](#outlinecolor "Direct link to outlineColor")

Type: `string`

Inactive outline color of the input.

### activeOutlineColor[​](#activeoutlinecolor "Direct link to activeOutlineColor")

Type: `string`

Active outline color of the input.

### textColor[​](#textcolor "Direct link to textColor")

Type: `string`

Color of the text in the input.

### dense[​](#dense "Direct link to dense")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `false`

Sets min height with densed layout. For `TextInput` in `flat` mode
height is `64dp` or in dense layout - `52dp` with label or `40dp` without label.
For `TextInput` in `outlined` mode
height is `56dp` or in dense layout - `40dp` regardless of label.
When you apply `height` prop in style the `dense` prop affects only `paddingVertical` inside `TextInput`

### multiline[​](#multiline "Direct link to multiline")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `false`

Whether the input can have multiple lines.

### numberOfLines Android only[​](#numberoflines--android-only "Direct link to numberoflines--android-only")

Type: `number`

The number of lines to show in the input (Android only).

### onFocus[​](#onfocus "Direct link to onFocus")

Type: `(args: any) => void`

Callback that is called when the text input is focused.

### onBlur[​](#onblur "Direct link to onBlur")

Type: `(args: any) => void`

Callback that is called when the text input is blurred.

### render[​](#render "Direct link to render")

Type: `(props: RenderProps) => React.ReactNode`

Default value: `(props: RenderProps) => <NativeTextInput {...props} />`

Callback to render a custom input component such as `react-native-text-input-mask`
instead of the default `TextInput` component from `react-native`.

Example:

```
<TextInput
  label="Phone number"
  render={props =>
    <TextInputMask
      {...props}
      mask="+[00] [000] [000] [000]"
    />
  }
/>
```

### value[​](#value "Direct link to value")

Type: `string`

Value of the text input.

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: [`StyleProp<TextStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/text-style-props)

Pass `fontSize` prop to modify the font size inside `TextInput`.
Pass `height` prop to set `TextInput` height. When `height` is passed,
`dense` prop will affect only input's `paddingVertical`.
Pass `paddingHorizontal` to modify horizontal padding.
This can be used to get MD Guidelines v1 TextInput look.

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

testID to be used on tests.

### contentStyle[​](#contentstyle "Direct link to contentStyle")

Type: [`StyleProp<TextStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/text-style-props)

Pass custom style directly to the input itself.
Overrides input style
Example: `paddingLeft`, `backgroundColor`

### outlineStyle[​](#outlinestyle "Direct link to outlineStyle")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

Pass style to override the default style of outlined wrapper.
Overrides style when mode is set to `outlined`
Example: `borderRadius`, `borderColor`

### underlineStyle[​](#underlinestyle "Direct link to underlineStyle")

Type: [`StyleProp<ViewStyle>`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/view-style-props)

Pass style to override the default style of underlined wrapper.
Overrides style when mode is set to `flat`
Example: `borderRadius`, `borderColor`

### editable[​](#editable "Direct link to editable")

Type:

Default value: `true`

## Known Issues[​](#known-issues "Direct link to Known Issues")

Details

* [Outline overlaps label](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/issues/3759#issuecomment-1601235262)
* [Long text wraps to a second line](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/issues/2581#issuecomment-790251987)

# TextInput.Affix

A component to render a leading / trailing text in the TextInput

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/textinput-outline.affix.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { TextInput } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [text, setText] = React.useState('');  
  
  return (  
    <TextInput  
      mode="outlined"  
      label="Outlined input"  
      placeholder="Type something"  
      right={<TextInput.Affix text="/100" />}  
    />  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/ToggleButton/

# ToggleButton

Toggle buttons can be used to group related options. To emphasize groups of related toggle buttons,
a group should share a common container.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/toggle-button.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { ToggleButton } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const ToggleButtonExample = () => {  
  const [status, setStatus] = React.useState('checked');  
  
  const onButtonToggle = value => {  
    setStatus(status === 'checked' ? 'unchecked' : 'checked');  
  };  
  
  return (  
    <ToggleButton  
      icon="bluetooth"  
      value="bluetooth"  
      status={status}  
      onPress={onButtonToggle}  
    />  
  );  
};  
  
export default ToggleButtonExample;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### icon (required)[​](#icon-required "Direct link to icon (required)")

Type: [`IconSource`](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/blob/main/src/components/Icon.tsx#L16)

Icon to display for the `ToggleButton`.

### size[​](#size "Direct link to size")

Type: `number`

Size of the icon.

### iconColor[​](#iconcolor "Direct link to iconColor")

Type: `string`

Custom text color for button.

### rippleColor[​](#ripplecolor "Direct link to rippleColor")

Type: `ColorValue`

Color of the ripple effect.

### disabled[​](#disabled "Direct link to disabled")

Type: `boolean`

Whether the button is disabled.

### accessibilityLabel[​](#accessibilitylabel "Direct link to accessibilityLabel")

Type: `string`

Accessibility label for the `ToggleButton`. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the button.

### onPress[​](#onpress "Direct link to onPress")

Type: `(value?: GestureResponderEvent | string) => void`

Function to execute on press.

### value[​](#value "Direct link to value")

Type: `string`

Value of button.

### status[​](#status "Direct link to status")

Type: `'checked' | 'unchecked'`

Status of button.

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: `Animated.WithAnimatedValue<StyleProp<ViewStyle>>`

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

### ref[​](#ref "Direct link to ref")

Type: `React.RefObject<View>`

### testID[​](#testid "Direct link to testID")

Type: `string`

testID to be used on tests.

* [Usage](#usage)

  + [icon (required)](#icon-required)
  + [size](#size)
  + [iconColor](#iconcolor)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/ToggleButton/ToggleButtonGroup

On this page

# ToggleButton.Group

Toggle group allows to control a group of toggle buttons.
It doesn't change the appearance of the toggle buttons. If you want to group them in a row, check out [ToggleButton.Row](/react-native-paper/docs/components/ToggleButton/ToggleButtonRow).

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/toggle-button-group.gif)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { ToggleButton } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => {  
  const [value, setValue] = React.useState('left');  
  
  return (  
    <ToggleButton.Group  
      onValueChange={value => setValue(value)}  
      value={value}>  
      <ToggleButton icon="format-align-left" value="left" />  
      <ToggleButton icon="format-align-right" value="right" />  
    </ToggleButton.Group>  
  );  
};  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### onValueChange (required)[​](#onvaluechange-required "Direct link to onValueChange (required)")

Type: `(value: Value) => void`

Function to execute on selection change.

### value (required)[​](#value-required "Direct link to value (required)")

Type: `Value | null`

Value of the currently selected toggle button.

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactNode`

React elements containing toggle buttons.

* [Usage](#usage)
* [Props](#props)
  + [onValueChange (required)](#onvaluechange-required)
  + [value (required)](#value-required)
  + [children (required)](#children-required)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/Tooltip/

On this page

# Tooltip

Tooltips display informative text when users hover over, focus on, or tap an element.

Plain tooltips, when activated, display a text label identifying an element, such as a description of its function. Tooltips should include only short, descriptive text and avoid restating visible UI text.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/tooltip.png)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { IconButton, Tooltip } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => (  
  <Tooltip title="Selected Camera">  
    <IconButton icon="camera" selected size={24} onPress={() => {}} />  
  </Tooltip>  
);  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `React.ReactElement`

Tooltip reference element. Needs to be able to hold a ref.

### enterTouchDelay[​](#entertouchdelay "Direct link to enterTouchDelay")

Type: `number`

Default value: `500`

The number of milliseconds a user must touch the element before showing the tooltip.

### leaveTouchDelay[​](#leavetouchdelay "Direct link to leaveTouchDelay")

Type: `number`

Default value: `1500`

The number of milliseconds after the user stops touching an element before hiding the tooltip.

### title (required)[​](#title-required "Direct link to title (required)")

Type: `string`

Tooltip title

### titleMaxFontSizeMultiplier[​](#titlemaxfontsizemultiplier "Direct link to titleMaxFontSizeMultiplier")

Type: `number`

Specifies the largest possible scale a title font can reach.

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

## Theme colors[​](#theme-colors "Direct link to Theme colors")

info

The table below outlines the theme colors, specifically for MD3 *(theme version 3)* at the moment.

| mode | backgroundColor | textColor |
| --- | --- | --- |
| - | theme.colors.onSurface | theme.colors.surface |

tip

If a dedicated prop for a specific color is not available or the `style` prop does not allow color modification, you can customize it using the `theme` prop. It allows to override any color, within the component, based on the table above.

*Example of overriding* `primary` *color:*

`<Tooltip theme={{ colors: { primary: 'green' } }} />`

* [Usage](#usage)
* [Props](#props)
  + [children (required)](#children-required)
  + [enterTouchDelay](#entertouchdelay)
  + [leaveTouchDelay](#leavetouchdelay)
  + [title (required)](#title-required)
  + [titleMaxFontSizeMultiplier](#titlemaxfontsizemultiplier)
  + [theme](#theme)
* [Theme colors](#theme-colors)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/TouchableRipple/

On this page

# TouchableRipple

A wrapper for views that should respond to touches.
Provides a material "ink ripple" interaction effect for supported platforms (>= Android Lollipop).
On unsupported platforms, it falls back to a highlight effect.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/touchable-ripple.gif)

## Usage[​](#usage "Direct link to Usage")

```
import * as React from 'react';  
import { View } from 'react-native';  
import { Text, TouchableRipple } from 'react-native-paper';  
  
const MyComponent = () => (  
  <TouchableRipple  
    onPress={() => console.log('Pressed')}  
    rippleColor="rgba(0, 0, 0, .32)"  
  >  
    <Text>Press anywhere</Text>  
  </TouchableRipple>  
);  
  
export default MyComponent;
```

## Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

### Pressable props[​](#pressable-props "Direct link to Pressable props")

*Extends:* [`...Pressable props`](https://reactnative.dev/docs/Pressable#props)

### borderless[​](#borderless "Direct link to borderless")

Type: `boolean`

Default value: `false`

Whether to render the ripple outside the view bounds.

### background[​](#background "Direct link to background")

Type: `Object`

Type of background drawabale to display the feedback (Android).
<https://reactnative.dev/docs/pressable#rippleconfig>

### centered[​](#centered "Direct link to centered")

Type: `boolean`

Whether to start the ripple at the center (Web).

### disabled[​](#disabled "Direct link to disabled")

Type: `boolean`

Whether to prevent interaction with the touchable.

### onPress[​](#onpress "Direct link to onPress")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Function to execute on press. If not set, will cause the touchable to be disabled.

### onLongPress[​](#onlongpress "Direct link to onLongPress")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Function to execute on long press.

### onPressIn[​](#onpressin "Direct link to onPressIn")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Function to execute immediately when a touch is engaged, before `onPressOut` and `onPress`.

### onPressOut[​](#onpressout "Direct link to onPressOut")

Type: `(e: GestureResponderEvent) => void`

Function to execute when a touch is released.

### rippleColor[​](#ripplecolor "Direct link to rippleColor")

Type: `ColorValue`

Color of the ripple effect (Android >= 5.0 and Web).

### underlayColor[​](#underlaycolor "Direct link to underlayColor")

Type: `string`

Color of the underlay for the highlight effect (Android < 5.0 and iOS).

### children (required)[​](#children-required "Direct link to children (required)")

Type: `| ((state: PressableStateCallbackType) => React.ReactNode)
| React.ReactNode`

Content of the `TouchableRipple`.

### style[​](#style "Direct link to style")

Type: `| StyleProp<ViewStyle>
| ((state: PressableStateCallbackType) => StyleProp<ViewStyle>)
| undefined`

### theme[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Type: [`ThemeProp`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/theming#theme-properties)

* [Usage](#usage)

  + [borderless](#borderless)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/bottom-navigation

On this page

# Using BottomNavigation with React Navigation

caution

The `createMaterialBottomTabNavigator` has been deprecated as of `[email protected]`. Instead, use `@react-navigation/bottom-tabs` version `7.x` or later, combined with `BottomNavigation.Bar` to achieve a Material Design look.

For implementation details, see the [dedicated example](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/BottomNavigation/BottomNavigationBar#with-react-navigation).

A material-design themed tab bar on the bottom of the screen that lets you switch between different routes with animation. Routes are lazily initialized - their screen components are not mounted until they are first focused.

This wraps the [`BottomNavigation`](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/components/BottomNavigation/) component from `react-native-paper`, however if you [configure the Babel plugin](https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/getting-started/), it won't include the whole library in your bundle.

![](/react-native-paper/screenshots/material-bottom-tabs.gif)

info

To use this navigator, ensure that you have [`@react-navigation/native` and its dependencies (follow this guide)](https://reactnavigation.org/docs/getting-started):

> 👉 For a complete example please visit `createMaterialBottomTabNavigator` [snack](https://snack.expo.dev/@react-native-paper/creatematerialbottomtabnavigator)

## API Definition[​](#api-definition "Direct link to API Definition")

To use this tab navigator, import it from `react-native-paper/react-navigation`:

```
import { createMaterialBottomTabNavigator } from 'react-native-paper/react-navigation';  
  
const Tab = createMaterialBottomTabNavigator();  
  
function MyTabs() {  
  return (  
    <Tab.Navigator>  
      <Tab.Screen name="Home" component={HomeScreen} />  
      <Tab.Screen name="Settings" component={SettingsScreen} />  
    </Tab.Navigator>  
  );  
}
```

> 👉 For a complete usage guide please visit [Tab Navigation](https://reactnavigation.org/docs/tab-based-navigation/)

### Props[​](#props "Direct link to Props")

The `Tab.Navigator` component accepts following props:

#### `id`[​](#id "Direct link to id")

Optional unique ID for the navigator. This can be used with [`navigation.getParent`](https://reactnavigation.org/docs/navigation-prop#getparent) to refer to this navigator in a child navigator.

#### `initialRouteName`[​](#initialroutename "Direct link to initialroutename")

The name of the route to render on first load of the navigator.

#### `screenOptions`[​](#screenoptions "Direct link to screenoptions")

Default options to use for the screens in the navigator.

#### `backBehavior`[​](#backbehavior "Direct link to backbehavior")

This controls what happens when `goBack` is called in the navigator. This includes pressing the device's back button or back gesture on Android.

It supports the following values:

* `firstRoute` - return to the first screen defined in the navigator (default)
* `initialRoute` - return to initial screen passed in `initialRouteName` prop, if not passed, defaults to the first screen
* `order` - return to screen defined before the focused screen
* `history` - return to last visited screen in the navigator; if the same screen is visited multiple times, the older entries are dropped from the history
* `none` - do not handle back button

#### `shifting`[​](#shifting "Direct link to shifting")

Whether the shifting style is used, the active tab icon shifts up to show the label and the inactive tabs won't have a label.

By default, this is `true` when you have more than 3 tabs. Pass `shifting={false}` to explicitly disable this animation, or `shifting={true}` to always use this animation.

#### `labeled`[​](#labeled "Direct link to labeled")

Whether to show labels in tabs. When `false`, only icons will be displayed.

#### `activeColor`[​](#activecolor "Direct link to activecolor")

Custom color for icon and label in the active tab.

#### `inactiveColor`[​](#inactivecolor "Direct link to inactivecolor")

Custom color for icon and label in the inactive tab.

#### `barStyle`[​](#barstyle "Direct link to barstyle")

Style for the bottom navigation bar. You can pass custom background color here:

```
<Tab.Navigator  
  initialRouteName="Home"  
  activeColor="#f0edf6"  
  inactiveColor="#3e2465"  
  barStyle={{ backgroundColor: '#694fad' }}  
>  
  {/* ... */}  
</Tab.Navigator>
```

If you have a translucent navigation bar on Android, you can also set a bottom padding here:

```
<Tab.Navigator  
  initialRouteName="Home"  
  activeColor="#f0edf6"  
  inactiveColor="#3e2465"  
  barStyle={{ paddingBottom: 48 }}  
>  
  {/* ... */}  
</Tab.Navigator>
```

#### `theme`[​](#theme "Direct link to theme")

Enables the customization of default theme attributes (e.g. colors) or facilitates the utilization of a personalized custom theme.

### Options[​](#options "Direct link to Options")

The following [options](https://reactnavigation.org/docs/screen-options) can be used to configure the screens in the navigator:

#### `title`[​](#title "Direct link to title")

Generic title that can be used as a fallback for `headerTitle` and `tabBarLabel`.

#### `tabBarIcon`[​](#tabbaricon "Direct link to tabbaricon")

Function that given `{ focused: boolean, color: string }` returns a React.Node, to display in the tab bar.

#### `tabBarColor` In v5.x works only with theme version 2. [​](#tabbarcolor-in-v5x-works-only-with-theme-version-2 "Direct link to tabbarcolor-in-v5x-works-only-with-theme-version-2")

Color for the tab bar when the tab corresponding to the screen is active. Used for the ripple effect. This is only supported when `shifting` is `true`.

#### `tabBarLabel`[​](#tabbarlabel "Direct link to tabbarlabel")

Title string of a tab displayed in the tab bar. When undefined, scene `title` is used. To hide, see `labeled` option in the previous section.

#### `tabBarBadge`[​](#tabbarbadge "Direct link to tabbarbadge")

Badge to show on the tab icon, can be `true` to show a dot, `string` or `number` to show text.

#### `tabBarAccessibilityLabel`[​](#tabbaraccessibilitylabel "Direct link to tabbaraccessibilitylabel")

Accessibility label for the tab button. This is read by the screen reader when the user taps the tab. It's recommended to set this if you don't have a label for the tab.

#### `tabBarTestID`[​](#tabbartestid "Direct link to tabbartestid")

ID to locate this tab button in tests.

### Events[​](#events "Direct link to Events")

The navigator can [emit events](https://reactnavigation.org/docs/navigation-events) on certain actions. Supported events are:

#### `tabPress`[​](#tabpress "Direct link to tabpress")

This event is fired when the user presses the tab button for the current screen in the tab bar. By default a tab press does several things:

* If the tab is not focused, tab press will focus that tab
* If the tab is already focused:
  + If the screen for the tab renders a scroll view, you can use [`useScrollToTop`](https://reactnavigation.org/docs/use-scroll-to-top) to scroll it to top
  + If the screen for the tab renders a stack navigator, a `popToTop` action is performed on the stack

To prevent the default behavior, you can call `event.preventDefault`:

```
React.useEffect(() => {  
  const unsubscribe = navigation.addListener('tabPress', (e) => {  
    // Prevent default behavior  
  
    e.preventDefault();  
    // Do something manually  
    // ...  
  });  
  
  return unsubscribe;  
}, [navigation]);
```

### Helpers[​](#helpers "Direct link to Helpers")

The tab navigator adds the following methods to the navigation prop:

#### `jumpTo`[​](#jumpto "Direct link to jumpto")

Navigates to an existing screen in the tab navigator. The method accepts following arguments:

* `name` - *string* - Name of the route to jump to.
* `params` - *object* - Screen params to pass to the destination route.

```
navigation.jumpTo('Profile', { name: 'Michaś' });
```

## Example[​](#example "Direct link to Example")

```
import { createMaterialBottomTabNavigator } from 'react-native-paper/react-navigation';  
import MaterialDesignIcons from '@react-native-vector-icons/material-design-icons';  
  
const Tab = createMaterialBottomTabNavigator();  
  
function MyTabs() {  
  return (  
    <Tab.Navigator  
      initialRouteName="Feed"  
      activeColor="#e91e63"  
      barStyle={{ backgroundColor: 'tomato' }}  
    >  
      <Tab.Screen  
        name="Feed"  
        component={Feed}  
        options={{  
          tabBarLabel: 'Home',  
          tabBarIcon: ({ color }) => (  
            <MaterialDesignIcons name="home" color={color} size={26} />  
          ),  
        }}  
      />  
      <Tab.Screen  
        name="Notifications"  
        component={Notifications}  
        options={{  
          tabBarLabel: 'Updates',  
          tabBarIcon: ({ color }) => (  
            <MaterialDesignIcons name="bell" color={color} size={26} />  
          ),  
        }}  
      />  
      <Tab.Screen  
        name="Profile"  
        component={Profile}  
        options={{  
          tabBarLabel: 'Profile',  
          tabBarIcon: ({ color }) => (  
            <MaterialDesignIcons name="account" color={color} size={26} />  
          ),  
        }}  
      />  
    </Tab.Navigator>  
  );  
}
```

* [API Definition](#api-definition)
  + [Props](#props)
  + [Options](#options)
  + [Events](#events)
  + [Helpers](#helpers)
* [Example](#example)

# Page: https://callstack.github.io/react-native-paper/docs/guides/contributing

# Contributing

# Contributing to React Native Paper

## Code of Conduct[​](#code-of-conduct "Direct link to Code of Conduct")

We want this community to be friendly and respectful to each other. Please read [the full text](https://callstack.com/code-of-conduct/?utm_source=github.com&utm_medium=referral&utm_campaign=react-native-paper&utm_term=code-of-conduct) so that you can understand what actions will and will not be tolerated.

## Our Development Process[​](#our-development-process "Direct link to Our Development Process")

The core team works directly on GitHub and all work is public.

### Development workflow[​](#development-workflow "Direct link to Development workflow")

> **Working on your first pull request?** You can learn how from this *free* series: [How to Contribute to an Open Source Project on GitHub](https://egghead.io/courses/how-to-contribute-to-an-open-source-project-on-github).

1. Fork the repo and create your branch from `main` (a guide on [how to fork a repository](https://help.github.com/articles/fork-a-repo/)).
2. Run `yarn` on the root level, to setup the development environment.
3. Do the changes you want and test them out in the example app before sending a pull request.

### Commit message convention[​](#commit-message-convention "Direct link to Commit message convention")

We follow the [conventional commits specification](https://www.conventionalcommits.org/en) for our commit messages:

* `fix`: bug fixes, e.g. fix Button color on DarkTheme.
* `feat`: new features, e.g. add Snackbar component.
* `refactor`: code refactor, e.g. new folder structure for components.
* `docs`: changes into documentation, e.g. add usage example for Button.
* `test`: adding or updating tests, eg unit, snapshot testing.
* `chore`: tooling changes, e.g. change circleci config.
* `BREAKING CHANGE`: for changes that break existing usage, e.g. change API of a component.

Our pre-commit hooks verify that your commit message matches this format when committing.

### Linting and tests[​](#linting-and-tests "Direct link to Linting and tests")

We use `typescript` for type checking, `eslint` with `prettier` for linting and formatting the code, and `jest` for testing. Our pre-commit hooks verify that the linter and tests pass when commiting. You can also run the following commands manually:

* `yarn typescript`: type-check files with `tsc`.
* `yarn lint`: lint files with `eslint` and `prettier`.
* `yarn test`: run unit tests with `jest`.

### Sending a pull request[​](#sending-a-pull-request "Direct link to Sending a pull request")

When you're sending a pull request:

* Prefer small pull requests focused on one change.
* Verify that `typescript`, `eslint` and all tests are passing.
* Preview the documentation to make sure it looks good.
* Follow the pull request template when opening a pull request.

When you're working on a component:

* Follow the guidelines described in the [official material design docs](https://material.io/guidelines/).
* Write a brief description of every prop when defining `type Props` to aid with documentation.
* Provide an example usage for the component (check other components to get a idea).
* Update the type definitions for Flow and TypeScript if you changed an API or added a component.

### Running the example[​](#running-the-example "Direct link to Running the example")

The example app uses [Expo](https://expo.dev/) for the React Native example. You will need to install the Expo app for [Android](https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=host.exp.exponent) and [iOS](https://itunes.apple.com/app/apple-store/id982107779) to start developing.

> [!IMPORTANT]  
> The example app is built with `[email protected]` and Expo SDK 52, which isn’t compatible with Expo Go. To run the app, you have to create a [development build](https://docs.expo.dev/develop/development-builds/create-a-build/).

After you're done, you can run `yarn example start` in the project root (or `npx expo start` in the `example/` folder) and scan the QR code to launch it on your device.

To run the example on web, run `yarn example web` in the project root.

### Testing a specific pull request/commit[​](#testing-a-specific-pull-requestcommit "Direct link to Testing a specific pull request/commit")

If you want to test the changes brought by a pull request, you can do so by pointing at the git-commit or branch in your `package.json` file. For example:

```
{  
  "dependencies": {  
    "react-native-paper": "git+https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper.git#<commit-hash>",  
  }  
}
```

Then run `yarn install`/`npm install` in your project to install the package from the git repository.

Alternatively, you may clone the `react-native-paper` repo and use the [yalc](https://github.com/wclr/yalc) tool to link the package to the project.

### Working on documentation[​](#working-on-documentation "Direct link to Working on documentation")

The documentation is automatically generated from the [TypeScript](https://www.typescriptlang.org/) annotations in the components. You can add comments above the type annotations to add descriptions. To preview the generated documentation, run `yarn docs start` in the project root.

### Publishing a release[​](#publishing-a-release "Direct link to Publishing a release")

We use [release-it](https://github.com/webpro/release-it) to automate our release. If you have publish access to the NPM package, run the following from the main branch to publish a new release:

```
yarn release
```

NOTE: You must have a `GITHUB_TOKEN` environment variable available. You can create a GitHub access token with the "repo" access [here](https://github.com/settings/tokens).

## Reporting issues[​](#reporting-issues "Direct link to Reporting issues")

You can report issues on our [bug tracker](https://github.com/callstack/react-native-paper/issues). Please follow the issue template when opening an issue.

## License[​](#license "Direct link to License")

By contributing to React Native Paper, you agree that your contributions will be licensed under its **MIT** license.
